### Question 151: GIBILL-11

**Query:** What is Chapter 35 DEA?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 4.64s

**Answer:**

Chapter 35 DEA (Dependents' Educational Assistance) is a program that provides education benefits to the spouse and dependent children (including step and adopted children) of a Veteran or Servicemember who meets certain criteria. These criteria include:

- The Veteran is permanently and totally disabled from service-connected conditions;
- The Veteran died in service;
- The Veteran died of service-connected causes; or
- The Veteran is currently missing in action or captured in the line of duty¹.

The benefit can be used for pursuing undergraduate or graduate degrees, courses leading to certificates or diplomas from business, technical, or vocational schools, apprenticeship, and on-the-job training programs. Correspondence courses benefits are available to spouses only. Each dependent gets their own individual entitlement of the benefit, which is paid directly to the dependent. The program provides up to 45 months of education or training for beneficiaries who used their Chapter 35 benefits before August 1, 2018, and 36 months for those who use the benefits on or after that date².

Additional notes include that children cannot receive DIC (Dependency and Indemnity Compensation) and DEA at the same time, and the benefit cannot be used for flight school but can be used for overseas programs².

Eligibility requirements for dependent children and spouses vary depending on when the event that made them eligible occurred, with different rules applying for events before or after August 1, 2023³⁴⁶.

**Sources:**
¹ [Chapter 35 (Dependents' Educational Assistance - DEA)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/pnt)

⁴ [Eligibility Requirements for Dependent Children (Historical) - (notes)](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)  
⁶ [Eligibility Requirements for Dependent Spouses (Historical) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/time)

### Question 152: GIBILL-12

**Query:** How long do GI Bill benefits last?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 3.75s

**Answer:**

The duration of GI Bill education benefits varies by the type of GI Bill:

- **Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill - Active Duty):** Benefits are generally payable for **10 years** following your release from honorable active service¹ ⁶.

- **Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill):** Provides up to **36 months** of education benefits. Veterans discharged before January 1, 2013, have **15 years** to use this benefit, but if discharged after January 1, 2013, there is **no time limit** to use the benefit² ³ ⁴.

### Question 153: GIBILL-13

**Query:** Can I use GI Bill for graduate school?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 2.68s

**Answer:**

Yes, you can use GI Bill education benefits, including Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill - Active Duty) and Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill), for graduate school.

- Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill) benefits may be used for college degree programs, which includes graduate degrees¹.
- Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill) provides education benefits for approved programs at institutions of higher learning, which includes graduate school programs².

Therefore, both the Montgomery GI Bill and Post-9/11 GI Bill can be applied toward graduate school education.

### Question 154: GIBILL-14

**Query:** What is the book stipend?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 2.32s

**Answer:**

The book stipend is an amount of up to $1,000 each year that you may receive to cover books and supplies. This amount is prorated if you are enrolled less than full time¹.

### Question 156: GIBILL-16

**Query:** What is the Post-9/11 GI Bill eligibility?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 4.35s

**Answer:**

The eligibility for the Post-9/11 GI Bill includes:

- Having an honorable period of Active Duty service on or after September 10, 2001.
- Certain members of the Reserves who lost education benefits when REAP was sunset in November 2015 may also be eligible to receive restored benefits under the Post-9/11 GI Bill.
- Veterans discharged before January 1, 2013, have 15 years to use this benefit.
- Veterans discharged after January 1, 2013, have no time limit to use the benefit.
- If a veteran received a discharge other than honorable, eligibility depends on whether they reenlisted once or had an appropriate prior period of honorable service. If so, they may still qualify, but benefits may be prorated if the service periods were shorter than the time needed to earn full entitlement⁷.

### Question 157: GIBILL-17

**Query:** Can I use GI Bill for vocational training?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 7.71s

**Answer:**

Yes, you can use GI Bill education benefits under both Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill - Active Duty) and Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill) for vocational training.

- Under Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill), benefits may be used for technical or vocational courses, among other types of training such as college degrees, flight training, apprenticeships, on-the-job training, licensing and certification tests, and entrepreneurship training¹.

- Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill) provides up to 36 months of education benefits for approved programs, which can include vocational training, though the context does not explicitly list vocational training, it does mention that it covers various education programs including institutions of higher learning and training¹.

Therefore, vocational training is explicitly covered under Chapter 30 and can be covered under Chapter 33 if the program is approved.

### Question 158: GIBILL-18

**Query:** What happens to unused GI Bill benefits?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 5.56s

**Answer:**

Unused GI Bill education benefits under Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill - Active Duty) generally expire 10 years following your release from honorable active service¹. For Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill), veterans discharged before January 1, 2013, have 15 years to use the benefit, but if discharged after January 1, 2013, there is no time limit to use the benefits².

Regarding switching from Chapter 30 to Chapter 33, if you exhaust all 36 months of the Post-9/11 GI Bill benefits, you will get your $1,200 contribution back in your final Monthly Housing Allowance (MHA) payment. However, if you are not receiving MHA in your final month, you will not get this money back automatically³.

Additionally, a Supreme Court decision on April 16, 2024, allows veterans who served at least two qualifying periods (including reenlistment without a break in service) for both Chapter 30 and Chapter 33 to potentially receive additional GI Bill benefits⁴.

³ [GI Bill Education Benefits - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibill#faq)  
⁴ [Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill (MGIB) - Active Duty) (Part 1)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibills#chapter30montgomeryg) and [Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill) (Part 1)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibills#chapter33post911gibi)

### Question 159: GIBILL-19

**Query:** Can I use GI Bill and VR&E together?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 5.58s

**Answer:**

You cannot use VR&E (Veterans Readiness and Employment) and DEA (Dependents' Educational Assistance) at the same time¹. However, regarding the use of GI Bill education benefits (such as Chapter 30 Montgomery GI Bill or Chapter 33 Post-9/11 GI Bill) with VR&E:

- Veterans have a lifetime limit of 48 months of GI Bill benefits.
- This limit does not prevent the Veteran from using other education benefits such as VR&E.
- Using your GI Bill before VR&E generally goes against the limit usages for VR&E unless the GI Bill usage is considered as having been under VR&E via retroactive induction. In that case, the VA would restore the GI Bill eligibility (months used) and count those months against the VR&E entitlement instead³.
- When using VR&E, you will need to apply for the Post 9/11 GI Bill to show eligibility or remaining entitlement to get the BAH rate, but you will not be using up any of your GI Bill entitlement by using VR&E².

So, while you cannot use VR&E and DEA simultaneously, you can use GI Bill benefits and VR&E, but there are specific rules about how the months of entitlement are counted and coordinated.

**Sources:**
¹ [Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E) Chapter 31 - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#faq)  
² [Other Benefits of VRE (Part 3)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#otherbenefitsofvre)  
³ [GI Bill Education Benefits](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibill#gibilleducationbenefits)

**Sources Cited:**

### Question 160: GIBILL-20

**Query:** What is the Forever GI Bill?

**Category:** GIBILL

**Response Time:** 7.02s

**Answer:**

The "Forever GI Bill" refers to the Post-9/11 GI Bill (Chapter 33) education benefits, which provide up to 36 months of education benefits to veterans who served on active duty after September 10, 2001. Key features of the Forever GI Bill include:

- There is **no time limit** to use the benefits if the veteran was discharged after January 1, 2013. Veterans discharged before that date have 15 years to use the benefit¹⁴.
- Benefits cover full tuition and mandatory fees paid directly to public schools, with capped rates for private or foreign schools. Additional programs like the Yellow Ribbon Program may help cover extra costs at private institutions¹⁶.
- Veterans attending at least one class in a classroom may receive a housing allowance equal to the military BAH for an E-5 with dependents at the school location¹.
- The Forever GI Bill can be combined with Montgomery GI Bill (Chapter 30) benefits if the veteran served at least two qualifying periods of service, potentially allowing for additional GI Bill benefits⁵.

The Montgomery GI Bill (Chapter 30) provides up to 36 months of a monthly stipend for education and training, generally payable for 10 years following honorable discharge. It can be used for various educational programs and includes options like a $600 Buy-Up Program to increase benefits and a kicker for critical shortage MOS³⁵.

In summary, the Forever GI Bill primarily refers to the Post-9/11 GI Bill with its expanded and extended benefits, including the removal of the time limit for use after 2013, and it can be combined with Montgomery GI Bill benefits under certain conditions⁵.

**Sources:**
¹ [Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill) (Part 1)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibills#chapter33post911gibi)  
² [Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill (MGIB) - Active Duty) (Part 1)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibills#chapter30montgomeryg)  
³ [Chapter 30 (Montgomery GI Bill (MGIB) - Active Duty) (Part 3)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibills#chapter30montgomeryg)  
⁴ [Chapter 33 (Post-9/11 GI Bill) (Part 2)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/gibills#chapter33post911gibi)

### Question 165: VRE-5

**Query:** What disability rating do I need for VR&E?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 2.77s

**Answer:**

To be eligible for Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E), also known as Chapter 31, you need to have at least a 20% disability rating and an employment handicap. Additionally, you must not have received a dishonorable discharge¹.

### Question 167: VRE-7

**Query:** What does VR&E pay for?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 3.41s

**Answer:**

Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E), also known as Chapter 31, is a VA program designed to help Veterans, Servicemembers, and certain eligible dependents attain employment. It is primarily an employment program rather than just a means to obtain a graduate-level degree¹.

While the context does not provide a detailed list of all specific payments VR&E covers, it does mention that VR&E includes a housing allowance paid monthly in arrears, with payments processed by the Treasury Department within a 10-business-day window around the end of each month⁶.

In summary, VR&E pays for services and support aimed at helping veterans achieve employment, which can include education and training, and it also provides a housing allowance during participation in the program.

### Question 170: VRE-10

**Query:** What are the VR&E tracks?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 7.2s

**Answer:**

The VR&E (Veterans Readiness and Employment) program offers five tracks to help Veterans attain employment:

1. **Reemployment**  
   - Assists Veterans in regaining employment with their former employer.  
   - May include employer assistance or equipment to accommodate the Veteran.  
   - Only used if the former job is still suitable considering the Veteran's disabilities.  

2. **Rapid Access to Employment**  
   - For Veterans who already have the skills, experience, and education needed for their desired field but face difficulties finding employment.  
   - Provides assistance such as job hunting, career counseling, interview preparation, and resume help.  
   - May include short-term certification training if needed.  

3. **Self-Employment**  
   - For Veterans who want to start their own business.  
   - Includes support in developing a business plan, training in small-business operations, marketing, finances, and tuition assistance for needed certifications/licenses.  

4. **Employment Through Long-Term Services**  
   - For Veterans needing additional training or assistance to obtain and maintain long-term employment.  
   - Offers tools like job hunting assistance, career guidance, higher education (undergraduate and graduate), job skill assessment, vocational training, apprenticeships, and on-the-job training.  
   - Note: VR&E is primarily an employment program, not an education program, so approval for advanced degrees like a Master's may be difficult if employment is reasonably attainable with current education.  

5. **Independent Living**  
   - For Veterans whose service-connected disabilities limit their ability to perform daily living activities and who cannot return to work immediately.  
   - Requires advanced eligibility: serious employment handicap, disabilities preventing work, and need for independent living services.  
   - May be used alongside efforts to obtain employment.  

These tracks are designed to address different Veteran needs in achieving employment or independent living goals through tailored services and support³⁴⁵.

**Sources:**  
¹ [Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E) Chapter 31 - (employment)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#veteransreadinessandemploymentvrechapter31)  
² [Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E) - (overview)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre)  
³ [Tracks - (employment)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)  
⁴ [Tracks (Part 2) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)  
⁵ [Tracks (Part 1) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E) Chapter 31](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#veteransreadinessandemploymentvrechapter31)
- [Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre)
- [Tracks](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)
- [Tracks (Part 2)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)
- [Tracks (Part 1)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)
- [References (Part 2)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#references)
- [Veterans Readiness and Employment (VR&E) Chapter 31 - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#faq)

### Question 171: VRE-11

**Query:** What is the employment track?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 5.21s

**Answer:**

The "employment track" refers to the various pathways Veterans can take through the Vocational Rehabilitation and Employment (VRE) program to gain or regain employment. There are five specific tracks:

1. **Reemployment**: Helps Veterans return to their former employer, possibly with accommodations for disabilities. This track is only used if the former job is still suitable given the Veteran's disabilities.

2. **Rapid Access to Employment**: For Veterans who already have the skills and education needed but are having trouble finding a job. Services include job hunting assistance, career counseling, interview preparation, resume help, and possibly short-term certification training.

3. **Self-Employment**: For Veterans who want to start their own business. Counseling includes business concept analysis, training in small-business operations, marketing, finances, and tuition assistance for certifications.

4. **Employment Through Long-Term Services**: For Veterans needing additional training or assistance to obtain and maintain long-term employment. Services include job hunting, career guidance, higher education, job skill assessment, apprenticeships, and vocational training.

5. **Independent Living**: For Veterans whose disabilities limit daily living activities and prevent them from working immediately. This track requires serious employment handicap and need for independent living services, and can be used alongside efforts to obtain employment.

These tracks provide tailored support depending on the Veteran's situation and goals in employment³.

**Sources:**
¹ [Tracks (Part 1) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)  
² [Tracks - (employment)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)  
³ [Tracks (Part 2) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Tracks (Part 1)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)
- [Tracks](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)
- [Tracks (Part 2)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#tracks)

### Question 173: VRE-13

**Query:** What is the independent living track?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 3.26s

**Answer:**

The Independent Living track is designed for Veterans whose service-connected disabilities limit their ability to perform activities of daily living, such as bathing, dressing, accessing the community, and interacting with others, and who cannot return to work right away. Veterans may use this track while also trying to obtain employment.

This track has advanced eligibility requirements:
- Must have a serious employment handicap; **AND**
- Disabilities prevent the Veteran from obtaining or returning to work; **AND**
- The Veteran needs services to live as independently as possible.

Examples of tools provided in this track include services to help Veterans live independently despite their disabilities.

### Question 174: VRE-14

**Query:** Can I use VR&E and GI Bill together?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 4.27s

**Answer:**

You cannot use VR&E and DEA (which is related to GI Bill benefits) at the same time¹. However, it is possible to use VR&E benefits without using up your GI Bill entitlement, meaning you can maintain your eligibility for GI Bill benefits while using VR&E². Additionally, it is possible for someone to use 48 months of VR&E benefits and then separately use 48 months of GI Bill benefits, indicating that the two programs have separate limits³⁴.

In summary:

- You cannot use VR&E and DEA (GI Bill) simultaneously¹.
- Using VR&E does not use up your GI Bill entitlement, so you can still apply for and use GI Bill benefits separately².
- You can use the full 48 months of VR&E benefits and separately use 48 months of GI Bill benefits³⁴.

### Question 175: VRE-15

**Query:** How long can I use VR&E benefits?

**Category:** VRE

**Response Time:** 2.82s

**Answer:**

You can use VR&E (Veterans Readiness and Employment) benefits for up to 48 months. However, this limit may be extended if special conditions are met. 

Additional important points include:
- If you used your GI Bill benefits before VR&E, that time counts against the 48-month limit.
- GI Bill eligibility months used before VR&E can possibly be restored via Retroactive Induction, potentially allowing you to use the GI Bill again.
- It is possible to use 48 months of VR&E benefits and then separately use 48 months of GI Bill benefits.
- Certain children of Vietnam Veterans and Veterans with covered service in Korea have a maximum eligibility of 24 months instead of 48 months.

¹ ²

**Sources:**
¹ [Duration of Program - (employment)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#durationofprogram)  
² [Duration of Program - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vre#durationofprogram)

### Question 176: CHAMPVA-1

**Query:** What is CHAMPVA?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 4.21s

**Answer:**

CHAMPVA, or the Civilian Health and Medical Program of the Department of Veterans Affairs, is a comprehensive health care program in which the VA shares the cost of covered health care services and supplies with eligible beneficiaries. It is designed to provide affordable health care coverage, featuring a $50 deductible per dependent (up to $100 maximum per family) and a maximum out-of-pocket amount of $3,000 per family annually. CHAMPVA pays amounts generally equivalent to Medicare/TRICARE rates for services and supplies and has specific rules regarding cost sharing and coordination with other insurance. It can also provide coverage overseas, with translation services arranged if needed³.

**Sources:**
¹ [Civilian Health and Medical Program of the Department of Veterans Affairs (CHAMPVA) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)  
² [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - (healthcare)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#champvahealthcareprogram)  
³ [CHAMPVA - (overview)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Civilian Health and Medical Program of the Department of Veterans Affairs (CHAMPVA)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)

- [CHAMPVA](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva)

- [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#faq)
- [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#faq)

### Question 177: CHAMPVA-2

**Query:** Who is eligible for CHAMPVA?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 5.21s

**Answer:**

CHAMPVA provides coverage to the following eligible beneficiaries:

- The spouse or widow(er) of a Veteran who:
  - Is rated Permanently and Totally disabled due to service-connected condition(s);
  - Was rated Permanently and Totally disabled due to service-connected condition(s) at the time of death;
  - Died due to a service-connected condition; or
  - Died on Active Duty and the dependents are not otherwise eligible for Department of Defense TRICARE benefits.

- Children of such Veterans, including:
  - Children aged 0-17;
  - Children aged 18-23 who are enrolled in school;
  - Children aged 18 or older who are classified as helpless.

- A Veteran's primary caregiver under the Program of Comprehensive Assistance for Family Caregivers (PCAFC), provided the caregiver does not have any other health insurance coverage.

Important eligibility notes include:

- The beneficiary cannot be eligible for TRICARE.
- Children who marry lose eligibility.
- In the event of divorce, entitlement for the former spouse ends effective the date of divorce.
- If entitlement is established due to the death of the Veteran or Servicemember, remarriage will end entitlement unless remarriage occurs on or after the beneficiary's 55th birthday, or if remarriage before age 55 ends, the beneficiary may reapply to reestablish the benefit⁴⁵.

**Sources:**
¹ [Eligibility - (healthcare)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#eligibility)  
² [Eligibility - (eligibility)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#eligibility)  
⁴ [Additional Eligibility - (healthcare)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#additionaleligibility)  
⁵ [Additional Eligibility - (eligibility)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#additionaleligibilit)

**Sources Cited:**

### Question 178: CHAMPVA-3

**Query:** What does CHAMPVA cover?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 2.53s

**Answer:**

CHAMPVA covers most health care services and supplies that are medically and psychologically necessary. However, dental care is not covered unless you also enroll in the VA Dental Insurance Program (VADIP). For detailed information on covered and non-covered services and supplies, beneficiaries receive a CHAMPVA Program Guide upon confirmation of eligibility. Additionally, pharmacy benefits are available, with more information accessible through the VA website. For a complete listing of non-covered services and supplies, the CHAMPVA Policy Manual can be consulted⁶.

### Question 179: CHAMPVA-4

**Query:** How do I apply for CHAMPVA?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 3.1s

**Answer:**

To apply for CHAMPVA, you can submit an application and supporting documents through one of the following methods:

- Online
- Fax
- Snail mail

You will need to include copies of relevant documents such as:

- Medicare card if the dependent qualifies for Medicare, or documentation from Social Security Administration if the dependent is 65 or older and does not qualify for Medicare.
- School certification of full-time enrollment for dependent children ages 18-23.
- Certificate of civil union, common-law marriage affidavit, or marriage certificate if you are a spouse or surviving spouse.
- Annulment decree, divorce decree, or death certificate if you are a surviving spouse who remarried before age 55 and your remarriage has ended.

To expedite processing, include copies of:

- Dependents’ birth certificate
- Benefits Letter showing the Veteran is permanently and totally disabled (or the death rating if you’re a survivor)
- Veteran’s DD214

For the online application, you can start by clicking the link provided on the VA website (not fully shown here)¹.

**Sources:**

¹ [Applying for CHAMPVA](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#applying)

### Question 180: CHAMPVA-5

**Query:** Is CHAMPVA the same as TRICARE?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 2.39s

**Answer:**

CHAMPVA is not the same as TRICARE. CHAMPVA is a health care program for eligible dependents and survivors of certain veterans, whereas TRICARE is a separate health insurance program primarily for active duty service members, retirees, and their families. Additionally, a dependent may be denied CHAMPVA if they are eligible for TRICARE, indicating that the two programs serve different populations and are distinct from each other¹³.

**Sources:**
¹ [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#faq)  
³ [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#faq)

### Question 183: CHAMPVA-8

**Query:** Can my spouse get CHAMPVA?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 3.57s

**Answer:**

Your spouse can get CHAMPVA coverage only if they are eligible as a spouse or caregiver of a Veteran who meets one of the following conditions:

- The Veteran is rated Permanently and Totally disabled due to service-connected condition(s);
- The Veteran was rated Permanently and Totally disabled due to service-connected condition(s) at the time of death;
- The Veteran died due to a service-connected condition; or
- The Veteran died on Active Duty and the dependents are not otherwise eligible for Department of Defense TRICARE benefits.

Additionally, the spouse cannot be eligible for TRICARE to qualify for CHAMPVA. If the spouse is divorced from the Veteran, entitlement ends effective the date of the divorce. If entitlement is established due to the death of the Veteran, remarriage generally ends entitlement unless remarriage occurs on or after the spouse's 55th birthday, or if remarriage before age 55 ends, the spouse may reapply to reestablish the benefit³.

**Sources:**
¹ [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#faq)  
² [Eligibility](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#eligibility)  
³ [Eligibility](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#eligibility)

### Question 186: CHAMPVA-11

**Query:** Can children use CHAMPVA?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 3.59s

**Answer:**

Yes, children can use CHAMPVA if they meet the eligibility criteria. CHAMPVA provides coverage to the children of a Veteran who:

- Are aged 0-17,
- Are aged 18-23 and enrolled in school,
- Or are 18 years or older and classified as a helpless child.

These children must be dependents of a Veteran who is rated permanently and totally disabled due to service-connected conditions, was rated permanently and totally disabled at the time of death, died due to a service-connected condition, or died on active duty with dependents not otherwise eligible for Department of Defense TRICARE benefits. 

Note that children who marry will lose eligibility for CHAMPVA coverage¹ ³ ⁵.

**Sources:**
¹ [CHAMPVA Healthcare Program - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#faq)  
³ [Eligibility - CHAMPVA](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#eligibility)

### Question 189: CHAMPVA-14

**Query:** Can I use CHAMPVA with Medicare?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 2.21s

**Answer:**

Yes, you can use CHAMPVA as secondary (supplemental) insurance if you have Medicare, because CHAMPVA can be secondary unless the other insurance is Medicaid, State Victims of Crime Compensation Programs, Indian Health Services, or Supplemental CHAMPVA policies. Medicare is not listed as an exception, so CHAMPVA can pay after Medicare does.

### Question 190: CHAMPVA-15

**Query:** What happens to CHAMPVA if I remarry?

**Category:** CHAMPVA

**Response Time:** 2.32s

**Answer:**

If you remarry and your CHAMPVA entitlement was established due to the death of a Veteran or Servicemember, your CHAMPVA coverage will end unless:

- Your remarriage takes place on or after your 55th birthday; or
- If you remarry before age 55 and your remarriage ends, you can reapply to reestablish the benefit.

Therefore, remarriage generally ends CHAMPVA entitlement except in these specific cases.

¹ [Eligibility - (healthcare)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/champva#eligibility)

### Question 191: 1151-1

**Query:** What is a 1151 claim?

**Category:** 1151

**Response Time:** 6.05s

**Answer:**

A 1151 claim is a type of VA disability claim that provides compensation for disabilities caused, worsened, or death resulting from the carelessness, negligence, lack of proper skill, error in judgment, or similar fault by the Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) during hospital care, medical or surgical treatment, examination, or participation in a compensated work therapy program. This includes aggravation of pre-existing conditions, new disabilities, and deaths caused by VA care or compensated work therapy programs¹⁴⁶.

To win a 1151 claim, the Veteran must show three elements:

1. An event involving VA fault (such as negligence or error in judgment).
2. Disability or death that began or worsened after this event.
3. A nexus letter or independent medical opinion linking the event to the disability or death.

There is no special form for filing a 1151 claim; the Veteran simply needs to identify the claim as a 1151 claim when filing with the VA. It is important to specify where and approximately when the event occurred and explain how the VA provider erred.

Additionally, 1151 claims can be filed for care received outside a VA Medical Center if the care was referred by the VA, the Veteran would not have suffered the disability/death but for the VA referral, and the VA's negligence caused the harm⁷.

**Sources:**
¹ [Winning a 1151 Claim - (claims_special)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winninga1151claim)  
² [Winning a 1151 Claim - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winninga1151claim)  
⁴ [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ - (faq)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)  
⁶ [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - (claims_special)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#38usc1151claimsvanegligence)  
⁷ [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ - (faq)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Winning a 1151 Claim](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winninga1151claim)
- [Winning a 1151 Claim](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winninga1151claim)
- [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)

### Question 192: 1151-2

**Query:** What is a federal tort claim?

**Category:** 1151

**Response Time:** 3.7s

**Answer:**

A federal tort claim is a claim filed by a Veteran who has been injured due to the negligence or wrongful act of a federal government employee acting within the scope of their official duties. To win such a claim, the Veteran must show:

- Injury caused by a federal government employee;
- The employee was acting within the scope of their official duties;
- The employee acted negligently or wrongfully; and
- The negligent or wrongful act proximately caused the injury complained of.

The claim must be submitted using Standard Form 95 to the Department of Veterans Affairs Office of General Counsel, Torts Law Group, and it must be received within 2 years of the injury. Unlike a 38 USC 1151 claim, the federal government has no duty to assist in gathering evidence for a federal tort claim, so the claimant must provide all necessary evidence themselves. It is highly recommended to seek an attorney who specializes in federal tort claims.

**Sources:**
¹ [Winning a Federal Tort Claim - (claims_special)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winningafederaltortclaim)  
² [Winning a Federal Tort Claim - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winningafederaltortc)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Winning a Federal Tort Claim](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winningafederaltortclaim)
- [Winning a Federal Tort Claim](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winningafederaltortc)
- [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#38usc1151claimsvanegligence)
- [1151 Claim](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151)
- [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)
- [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)

### Question 193: 1151-3

**Query:** Can I sue the VA for malpractice?

**Category:** 1151

**Response Time:** 4.57s

**Answer:**

Yes, you can sue the VA for malpractice through a Federal Tort Claim. To win such a claim, you must show:

- You were injured by a federal government employee;
- The employee was acting within the scope of their official duties;
- The employee acted negligently or wrongfully; and
- The negligent or wrongful act proximately caused your injury.

You or your legal representative can submit a claim using Standard Form 95 to the VA Office of General Counsel, Torts Law Group. It is highly recommended to seek an attorney who specializes in federal tort claims. Note that the claim must be received within 2 years of the injury, and unlike a 1151 claim, the federal government has no Duty to Assist, so you will need to gather and provide all evidence yourself¹⁴⁶.

Additionally, 38 USC 1151 claims cover disabilities or deaths caused by VA negligence, carelessness, or error in judgment during VA medical care or compensated work therapy programs. However, 1151 claims are different from Federal Tort Claims and have their own procedures and benefits²⁷.

**Sources:**

### Question 194: 1151-4

**Query:** How do I file a 1151 claim?

**Category:** 1151

**Response Time:** 3.13s

**Answer:**

To file a 1151 claim, you do not need a special or separate form. Instead, you should:

- File a regular VA disability claim.
- Clearly identify the claim as a 1151 claim when submitting it.
- Include the following key elements in your claim:
  1. Describe the event that caused the injury or disability, including where and approximately when it occurred.
  2. Show that a disability or death began or was made worse after the event.
  3. Provide a Nexus letter or independent medical opinion linking the event to the disability or death.
- Explain how the VA provider was negligent, careless, or made an error that caused the harm.

This information helps the VA obtain relevant records and properly evaluate your claim.

**Sources:**
¹ [Winning a 1151 Claim - (claims_special)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#winninga1151claim)

### Question 197: 1151-7

**Query:** What is VA negligence?

**Category:** 1151

**Response Time:** 2.53s

**Answer:**

VA negligence refers to carelessness, lack of proper skill, error in judgment, or similar fault on the part of the Department of Veterans Affairs in providing hospital care, medical or surgical treatment, examinations, or participation in compensated work therapy programs. This negligence can result in disabilities, aggravation of pre-existing conditions, new disabilities, or death caused by the VA's actions or omissions¹⁵.

### Question 198: 1151-8

**Query:** Can I get compensation for VA medical error?

**Category:** 1151

**Response Time:** 7.88s

**Answer:**

Yes, you can get compensation for a VA medical error under a 38 USC 1151 claim if certain conditions are met. Compensation can be paid for disabilities or death caused by VA carelessness, negligence, or error in judgment related to medical treatment or examinations. Specifically, compensation is available if:

- The disability or death resulted from VA acts of omission, such as failure to obtain informed consent prior to treatment or failure to provide timely diagnosis or treatment.

- There was an error in judgment involving negligence (not just a misdiagnosis or treatment that was later found incorrect).

- The disability or death was caused by VA examinations or compensated work therapy program participation under specific conditions.

- The VA carelessness or negligence directly resulted in the disability or death.

Additionally, if the VA referred you to a non-VA facility and the disability or death would not have occurred but for that referral and VA negligence, you may also be eligible for compensation.

Examinations for 1151 claims are conducted by third-party contractors to avoid conflicts of interest, and you can also provide your own medical opinion at your own cost.

You can also claim conditions that developed or were aggravated by a condition granted under 1151.

In summary, compensation for VA medical error is possible if the error was due to negligence or carelessness by the VA and caused or aggravated a disability or death³⁴⁶⁷.

**Sources:**

¹ [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)  
² [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)  
³ [38 USC 1151 Claims (VA Negligence) - FAQ](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#faq)  
⁴ [Detailed Explanation of Criteria](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/1151#detailedexplanationofcriteria)

### Question 201: AO-1

**Query:** What is Agent Orange?

**Category:** AO

**Response Time:** 2.58s

**Answer:**

Agent Orange is a herbicide and defoliant chemical used during military service, notably in the Vietnam War. Congress has recognized that Veterans who were exposed to Agent Orange are more likely to develop certain diseases. It is associated with health risks and conditions that the VA acknowledges for disability benefits purposes.

### Question 202: AO-2

**Query:** What conditions are presumptive for Agent Orange?

**Category:** AO

**Response Time:** 2.97s

**Answer:**

The conditions that are presumptive for Agent Orange exposure include:

- Chloracne or other acneform disease consistent with chloracne
- Early-onset peripheral neuropathy
- Porphyria cutanea tarda

These conditions must have developed within one year of the last possible exposure to Agent Orange and must have reached a severity of at least 10% within that year to be considered presumptive¹.

Additionally, based on the PACT Act, two new Agent Orange presumptive conditions have been added:

- High blood pressure (hypertension)
- Monoclonal gammopathy of undetermined significance (MGUS)

Other Agent Orange presumptive conditions include certain cancers, type 2 diabetes, and other illnesses, though specific details on these are not provided in the context².

**Sources:**
¹ [Presumptive Diseases - (presumptive)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#presumptivediseases)  
² [Vietnam era Veteran eligibility - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#vietnameraveteraneligibility)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Agent Orange Exposure](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#agentorangeexposure)
- [Agent Orange](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange)

### Question 203: AO-3

**Query:** What is the Nehmer rule?

**Category:** AO

**Response Time:** 4.66s

**Answer:**

⚠️ **Note:** My sources may not fully cover this topic. Our internal confidence score is **48.6%** for this response - please verify the answer with your own due diligence. A report has been generated and someone will review this.

The Nehmer rule refers to a VA policy under 38 CFR 3.816 that requires the VA to grant earlier effective dates for certain presumptive conditions related to Agent Orange exposure when those conditions were diagnosed before they became presumptive and the initial claim was filed before the condition was added to the presumptive list. Specifically:

- It applies to conditions named in 38 CFR 3.309(e) except chloracne.
- When a new presumptive condition is added, the VA must review prior decisions and grant earlier effective dates as appropriate.
- The rule allows veterans to receive service connection effective from the date of the initial claim if there was evidence of diagnosis before the condition became presumptive.
- Claims filed after the condition became presumptive are not subject to Nehmer but may still be eligible under liberalizing law.
- Some conditions like hypertension and MGUS are currently not eligible for Nehmer consideration.

For example, if a veteran filed a claim for lung cancer before it became presumptive and had medical evidence of diagnosis, the VA must grant service connection effective from the date of the initial claim, even if the claim was denied initially and later reopened after the condition became presumptive.

**Sources:**
¹ [Nehmer Class Members (38 CFR 3.816) (Part 4) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#nehmerclassmembers38)  
² [Nehmer Class Members (38 CFR 3.816) (Part 3) - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#nehmerclassmembers38)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Nehmer Class Members (38 CFR 3.816) (Part 4)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#nehmerclassmembers38)
- [Nehmer Class Members (38 CFR 3.816) (Part 3)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#nehmerclassmembers38)

### Question 204: AO-4

**Query:** Am I eligible for Agent Orange benefits?

**Category:** AO

**Response Time:** 6.58s

**Answer:**

You may be eligible for Agent Orange benefits if you meet the following criteria:

- You served in one of the specified locations during the eligible time periods, including:
  - Republic of Vietnam from January 9, 1962, through May 7, 1975 (including Brown Water Navy and Blue Water Navy service)
  - Thailand (any U.S. or Royal Thai military base) from January 9, 1962, through June 30, 1976
  - Laos from December 1, 1965, through September 30, 1969
  - Korean DMZ from September 1, 1967, through August 31, 1971
  - Guam and American Samoa (including territorial waters) from January 9, 1962, through July 30, 1980
  - Cambodia (at Mimot or Krek, Kampong Cham Province) from April 16, 1969, through April 30, 1969
  - Johnston Atoll or on a ship that called at Johnston Atoll from January 1, 1972, through September 30, 1977

- You served on active duty or as a reservist in an Air Force unit with a C-123 aircraft contaminated with Agent Orange and had repeated contact with the aircraft due to your duties.

- You have a presumptive condition recognized by the VA related to Agent Orange exposure, including new conditions added by the PACT Act such as high blood pressure (hypertension) and monoclonal gammopathy of undetermined significance (MGUS), as well as other recognized diseases like certain cancers and type 2 diabetes.

- There is no definitive evidence that you were not exposed to Agent Orange during your service.

If you meet these eligibility criteria and have a diagnosed condition related to Agent Orange exposure, you may apply for VA disability compensation and health care benefits. If your claim is denied, you can seek assistance from a Veterans Service Organization (VSO) to file an appeal³⁴⁵⁶.

### Question 207: AO-7

**Query:** Is Parkinson's connected to Agent Orange?

**Category:** AO

**Response Time:** 1.98s

**Answer:**

Yes, Parkinson's Disease is connected to Agent Orange exposure. It is recognized as a presumptive condition for veterans who were exposed to Agent Orange, meaning that if a veteran has Parkinson's Disease and was exposed to Agent Orange, the condition is presumed to be service-connected for VA disability purposes¹.

### Question 210: AO-10

**Query:** Where was Agent Orange used?

**Category:** AO

**Response Time:** 4.92s

**Answer:**

Agent Orange was used in the following locations during specific time periods:

- Republic of Vietnam (including Brown Water Navy Service and Blue Water Navy Service within 12 nautical miles seaward from the demarcation line of Vietnam, Cambodia) from January 9, 1962, through May 7, 1975
- American Samoa (including territorial waters) from January 9, 1962, through July 30, 1980
- Guam (including territorial waters) from January 9, 1962, through July 30, 1980
- Cambodia (at Mimot or Krek, Kampong Cham Province) from April 16, 1969, through April 30, 1969
- Johnston Atoll or on a ship that called at Johnston Atoll from January 1, 1972, through September 30, 1977
- Korean Demilitarized Zone (in or near) from September 1, 1967, through August 31, 1971
- Laos from December 1, 1965, through September 30, 1969
- Thailand (any U.S. or Royal Thai military base) from January 9, 1962, through June 30, 1976

These locations are recognized for presumptive exposure to Agent Orange based on service dates and locations¹³⁵.

### Question 211: DEPENDENTS-1

**Query:** Can I add dependents to my VA benefits?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 3.85s

**Answer:**

Yes, you can add dependents to your VA benefits. For example, you can add a new child as a dependent once they have a Social Security Number. After obtaining the SSN, you must claim them as a dependent and then apply to have them added to certain VA programs like CHAMPVA¹.

Additionally, dependents such as children and spouses may be eligible for benefits like Chapter 35 Dependents Educational Assistance (DEA), provided they meet specific eligibility criteria related to the timing of the Veteran's service or events, age, and schooling status² ⁴ ⁶.

However, dependent parents are generally not eligible for CHAMPVA coverage unless they are an appropriate caregiver³.

### Question 212: DEPENDENTS-2

**Query:** What is DIC (Dependency and Indemnity Compensation)?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 2.4s

**Answer:**

Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC) is a tax-free monetary benefit paid to eligible surviving family members of a Servicemember who died in the line of duty or a Veteran who died from a service-connected illness or injury. It also covers survivors of Veterans who died from conditions related to service but not formally service-connected during their lifetime, those who died due to VA medical care or participation in VA work programs, or those who were rated 100% disabled due to service-connected disabilities for a specified period before death. The benefit is intended to provide financial support to surviving spouses, children, or parents who meet certain eligibility criteria¹.

**Sources:**

### Question 213: DEPENDENTS-3

**Query:** How do I add my spouse to my benefits?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 3.05s

**Answer:**

To add your spouse to your benefits, you need to claim them as a dependent first. For example, if you have a new child, you must obtain their Social Security Number and claim them as a dependent before adding them to CHAMPVA. By analogy, for a spouse, you would similarly need to officially claim them as a dependent through the appropriate VA process before they can be added to your benefits¹.

Additionally, spouses remain eligible for certain benefits as long as the marriage is active, and surviving spouses have specific eligibility rules depending on remarriage status²³.

For applying to certain benefits like education benefits, the dependent (spouse) must apply from their own account once claimed as a dependent⁴.

### Question 214: DEPENDENTS-4

**Query:** What benefits do surviving spouses get?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 5.8s

**Answer:**

Surviving spouses of eligible Veterans are entitled to a variety of benefits, including:

- National Cemetery Burial benefits, even if the Veteran is not buried or memorialized in a national cemetery. Surviving spouses who remarry after January 1, 2000, to a non-Veteran remain eligible for burial benefits based on their prior marriage to the eligible Veteran¹⁴⁵.
- Eligibility for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC) if certain marriage and service conditions are met, with specific rules about remarriage affecting eligibility²⁷.
- Access to the Civilian Health and Medical Program of the Department of Veterans Affairs (CHAMPVA) for health care coverage⁵.
- Continuance of Claim/Appeal benefits for monetary claims⁵.
- Dependents Educational Assistance (DEA) for education benefits, which surviving spouses can access along with children⁵⁶.
- Educational and Career Counseling (Chapter 36) services⁵.
- Federal Civil Service Preference for employment opportunities⁵.
- Life Insurance benefits⁵.
- Medal of Honor Pension for eligible surviving spouses⁵.
- VA automobile allowance and adaptive equipment, Specially Adapted Housing grants, and potentially Special Monthly Compensation depending on disease progression⁶.
- Increased pension rates if the surviving spouse is housebound or requires aid and attendance¹.

Additionally, surviving spouses must meet certain income and net worth limits and must not remarry (with some exceptions) to maintain eligibility for some benefits¹.

### Question 215: DEPENDENTS-5

**Query:** What is Chapter 35 DEA?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 5.67s

**Answer:**

Chapter 35 DEA (Dependents' Educational Assistance) is a VA education benefit program that provides education and training opportunities to the spouse and dependent children (including step and adopted children) of a Veteran or Servicemember who meets certain criteria. These criteria include:

- The Veteran is permanently and totally disabled from service-connected conditions;
- The Veteran died in service;
- The Veteran died of service-connected causes; or
- The Veteran is currently missing in action or captured in the line of duty¹.

The program offers up to 36 months of education or training benefits for those using the benefit on or after August 1, 2018. It can be used for undergraduate or graduate degrees, certificate or diploma courses from business, technical or vocational schools, apprenticeships, and on-the-job training programs. Spouses may also use the benefit for correspondence courses. The benefit is paid directly to the dependent, and each dependent has their own individual entitlement².

Additional important notes include that children cannot receive both Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC) and DEA at the same time, and DEA benefits do not count against the maximum 48 months of educational benefits if the dependent is eligible for other education benefits².

Eligibility requirements vary depending on when the event that made the dependent eligible occurred, with different rules applying for events before or on/after August 1, 2023³⁴.

**Sources:**
¹ [Chapter 35 (Dependents' Educational Assistance - DEA)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/pnt)  
² [Benefit - (notes)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/mental)  
³ [Eligibility Requirements for Dependent Children and Spouses - (notes)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/ears)  
⁴ [Eligibility Requirements for Dependent Children (Historical) - (notes)](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

**Sources Cited:**

### Question 216: DEPENDENTS-6

**Query:** Can my children get VA benefits?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 6.1s

**Answer:**

Your children may be eligible for VA benefits depending on several factors related to your status as a Veteran and their circumstances:

- For CHAMPVA health coverage, children are eligible if the Veteran:
  - Is rated Permanently and Totally disabled due to service-connected conditions;
  - Was rated Permanently and Totally disabled due to service-connected conditions at the time of death;
  - Died due to a service-connected condition; or
  - Died on Active Duty and the dependents are not otherwise eligible for Department of Defense TRICARE benefits.

- Eligible children for CHAMPVA must be:
  - Aged 0-17, or
  - Aged 18-23 if enrolled in school, or
  - Aged 18+ if classified as a helpless child.

- Children who marry will lose CHAMPVA eligibility.

- For VA education benefits under Chapter 35 Dependents Educational Assistance (DEA):
  - Children may be eligible if they are dependents of a Veteran and eligible for any VA education benefit.
  - Eligibility criteria differ based on when the event making the child eligible occurred:
    - For events before August 1, 2023, children must be between 18-26 years old, and getting married does not end eligibility.
    - For events on or after August 1, 2023, the benefit does not expire, but spouses divorced from the Veteran lose eligibility.
  - Children cannot use DEA benefits while on Active Duty; eligibility may be extended but not past age 31.
  - Children attending approved high schools can use DEA benefits for up to 5 months until August 1, 2026.

- To apply for education benefits, the dependent child must apply from their own account and will receive a Certificate of Eligibility to present to their school's Certifying Official.

In summary, your children can get VA benefits such as CHAMPVA health coverage and educational assistance if they meet the eligibility criteria related to your Veteran status and their age, schooling, and marital status³⁴⁵⁶⁷.

**Sources:**

### Question 218: DEPENDENTS-8

**Query:** How do I apply for DIC?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 3.15s

**Answer:**

To apply for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC), follow these steps:

- If you are the surviving spouse or child of a Servicemember who died while on active duty, your military casualty assistance officer will assist you in completing an Application for DIC, Death Pension, and/or Accrued Benefits by a Surviving Spouse or Child using VA Form 21P-534a. The officer will help you mail the form to the correct VA regional office.

- If you are the surviving spouse or child of a Veteran, fill out an Application for DIC, Death Pension, and/or Accrued Benefits using VA Form 21P-534EZ. Mail this form to the Pension Management Center (PMC) for your state.

- If you are a surviving parent, fill out an Application for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation by Parent(s) using VA Form 21P-535 and mail it to the Pension Management Center (PMC) for your state.

- You can also upload the completed VA Form 21-534EZ online through the VA's secure portal.

These forms and instructions are available online for download and submission¹⁴.

**Sources:**
¹ [Applying - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)  
⁴ [Applying - (policy)](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Applying](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)
- [[Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC)](https://www.va.gov/disability/dependency-indemnity-compensation/)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/appeals)
- [Spouse](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/ears)
- [Applying](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Children](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/dependents#helpless)
- [Applying](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/life-insurance#top)
- [Applying](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)

### Question 219: DEPENDENTS-9

**Query:** What is survivor pension?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 2.5s

**Answer:**

A survivor pension is a monthly payment provided by the VA to qualified surviving spouses and unmarried dependent children of wartime Veterans. To be eligible, survivors must meet certain income and net worth limits set by Congress. The pension is designed to offer financial support to those who survive Veterans who served during wartime. However, payments will be stopped if the survivor is incarcerated for over 60 days due to a felony or misdemeanor conviction or is a fugitive felon. To apply for apportionment of the pension, VA Form 21-0788 must be completed and submitted to the VA by the surviving spouse or their dependents¹.

**Sources:**
¹ [Survivors Pension](https://www.va.gov/pension/survivors-pension/)

**Sources Cited:**
- [[Survivors Pension](https://www.va.gov/pension/survivors-pension/)](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Survivor Benefits](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/vaclaim)
- [[Survivor Benefit Plan](https://militarypay.defense.gov/Benefits/Survivor-Benefit-Program/Overview/)  / [Reserve Component Benefit Plan](https://www.dfas.mil/retiredmilitary/provide/rcsbp/)  (SBP)/(RCSBP)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)
- [Surviving Spouse](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/ears)

### Question 220: DEPENDENTS-10

**Query:** Can I get benefits if my veteran parent died?

**Category:** DEPENDENTS

**Response Time:** 5.15s

**Answer:**

Yes, you may be eligible for benefits if your veteran parent died. According to the information:

- Surviving parents can qualify for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC) payments if the veteran died from a service-connected disability¹.
- Parents may also qualify for a one-time accrued benefits payment if the veteran was owed unpaid benefits at the time of death¹.
- To be eligible as a surviving parent, you must be unmarried, or married to someone who is permanently and totally disabled, or legally separated from your spouse⁴.
- You can apply for these benefits by submitting an Application for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation by Parent(s) (VA Form 21P-535) to the Pension Management Center for your state⁶.

Additionally, surviving parents may be eligible for other benefits such as continuance of claim/appeal, life insurance, and federal civil service preference, but not for burial benefits or educational assistance that spouses and children receive⁵.

**Sources:**
¹ [Information for survivors - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#informationforsurvivors)  
⁴ [Parent of a Disabled or Deceased Veteran - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/survivorbenefits#top)  
⁵ [Benefit Summary - (policy)](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/appeals)  
⁶ [Applying - (policy)](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

**Sources Cited:**

### Question 221: BUDDY-1

**Query:** What is a buddy letter?

**Category:** BUDDY

**Response Time:** 2.17s

**Answer:**

A buddy letter is a statement written by someone who can attest to your military service, changes in your behavior, or the severity of your symptoms. It is used as evidence to support your VA disability claim, especially when military records are missing evidence or context. The person writing the buddy letter could be someone who served with you, a friend or family member, a civilian coworker or supervisor, or others such as a parole officer or priest. This letter helps provide additional context or proof related to your claim.

**Sources:**
¹ [Who Can Write a Buddy Letter/Statement?](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/buddy#whocanwriteabuddyletterstatement)  
² [Buddy Letters and Statements](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/buddy#buddylettersandstatements)

### Question 222: BUDDY-2

**Query:** Who can write a buddy statement?

**Category:** BUDDY

**Response Time:** 1.68s

**Answer:**

The following groups of people can write a buddy statement in support of your VA claim:

- Someone who served with you.
- Your friends and family.
- Civilian coworkers or supervisors.
- Anyone else such as your parole officer, priest, etc.¹

### Question 223: BUDDY-3

**Query:** What form do I use for a buddy letter?

**Category:** BUDDY

**Response Time:** 2.59s

**Answer:**

For a buddy letter, the preferred form is VA Form 21-10210. However, if you do not see this form available when uploading, you can select "Other Correspondence" as an option. Additionally, if your buddy uses VA Form 21-4138 instead, it is acceptable and you should not worry about resubmitting their statement, although it is best practice to use the latest and correct form⁵.

### Question 231: PACT-1

**Query:** What is the PACT Act?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 4.33s

**Answer:**

The PACT Act, or The Sergeant First Class (SFC) Heath Robinson Honoring our Promise to Address Comprehensive Toxics Act, is a law that expands VA health care and benefits for Veterans exposed to burn pits, Agent Orange, and other toxic substances. It is considered one of the largest health care and benefit expansions in VA history. The Act:

- Expands and extends eligibility for VA health care for Veterans with toxic exposures and Veterans of the Vietnam, Gulf War, and post-9/11 eras
- Adds over 20 more presumptive conditions related to burn pits, Agent Orange, and other toxic exposures
- Adds more presumptive-exposure locations for Agent Orange and radiation
- Requires VA to provide a toxic exposure screening to every Veteran enrolled in VA health care
- Helps improve research, staff education, and treatment related to toxic exposures

The PACT Act allows Veterans and survivors to file claims for related disability compensation and apply for VA health care, with expanded eligibility starting March 5, 2024, earlier than originally planned.

**Sources:**
¹ [PACT Act - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#pactact)  
² [What’s the PACT Act and how will it affect my VA benefits and care? - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#whatsthepactactandhowwillitaffectmyvabenefitsandcare)

**Sources Cited:**
- [PACT Act](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

### Question 232: PACT-2

**Query:** What conditions are presumptive under the PACT Act?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 3.0s

**Answer:**

The PACT Act adds over 20 presumptive conditions related to burn pits, Agent Orange, and other toxic exposures. It also expands presumptive-exposure locations for Agent Orange and radiation. However, the exact list of these presumptive conditions under the PACT Act is not detailed in the provided context.

More generally, presumptive conditions related to toxic exposure include various mental health conditions such as psychosis, depression, anxiety, and dementia (Alzheimer's disease) linked to traumatic brain injury (TBI), as well as conditions related to Gulf environmental hazards. These are examples of presumptive conditions but not specifically listed as part of the PACT Act presumptive conditions in the context provided¹⁴.

For the precise list of presumptive conditions under the PACT Act, you may need to consult the official VA resources directly.

### Question 233: PACT-3

**Query:** Am I eligible for PACT Act benefits?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 3.71s

**Answer:**

You may be eligible for PACT Act benefits if you meet the basic service and discharge requirements and any of the following apply to you:

- You served in the Vietnam War, the Gulf War, Iraq, Afghanistan, or any other combat zone after 9/11.
- You deployed in support of the Global War on Terror.
- You were exposed to toxins or other hazards during military service at home or abroad, including burn pits, sand and dust, particulates, oil well or sulfur fires, chemicals, radiation, warfare agents, depleted uranium, herbicides, and other occupational hazards.

Even if none of these descriptions apply, you may still be eligible for VA health care based on your service. The PACT Act expands and extends eligibility for VA health care for Veterans with toxic exposures and Veterans of the Vietnam, Gulf War, and post-9/11 eras, and adds many presumptive conditions related to toxic exposures.

You can apply for VA health care or file a disability claim related to the PACT Act benefits online or through other methods provided by the VA²⁵.

**Sources:**
¹ [Am I eligible for VA health care under the PACT Act?](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#amieligibleforvahealthcareunderthepactact)  
² [The PACT Act and your VA benefits](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#pactact)  
⁵ [Getting benefits](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#gettingbenefits)

**Sources Cited:**

- [Information for survivors](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [How the PACT Act affects Camp Lejeune claims and related benefits](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

### Question 235: PACT-5

**Query:** Does the PACT Act cover Gulf War veterans?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 4.31s

**Answer:**

Yes, the PACT Act covers Gulf War veterans. It expands and extends eligibility for VA health care for Veterans of the Gulf War era and post-9/11 eras, including those exposed to burn pits and other toxic substances. The Act adds more than 20 presumptive conditions related to burn pits and toxic exposures, such as various cancers and respiratory illnesses, specifically benefiting Gulf War era and post-9/11 Veterans¹⁵.

### Question 237: PACT-7

**Query:** How do I file a PACT Act claim?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 3.31s

**Answer:**

To file a PACT Act claim for a presumptive condition, you can:

- File a new disability claim online now if you have not filed a claim for the presumptive condition before. You can also file by mail, in person, or with the help of a trained professional.  
- If your previous claim was denied but your condition is now considered presumptive under the PACT Act, you can submit a Supplemental Claim to have your case reviewed again.  
- If you have a pending claim for a condition now considered presumptive, you do not need to take any action as VA will update your claim accordingly.  

You can start filing your claim online here: [File for VA disability compensation online](https://www.va.gov/disability/file-disability-claim-form-21-526ez/).

If you need assistance or more information about filing a claim, you can also call VA at 800-698-2411 (TTY: 711)¹.

**Sources:**
¹ [The PACT Act and your VA benefits](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#pactact)  
² [Getting benefits](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#gettingbenefits)

### Question 238: PACT-8

**Query:** What is a toxic exposure screening?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 3.09s

**Answer:**

A toxic exposure screening is a health assessment available at VA health facilities that asks Veterans if they believe they were exposed to certain hazardous substances during their military service. These hazards include open burn pits and other airborne hazards, Gulf War-related exposures, Agent Orange, radiation, Camp Lejeune contaminated water exposure, and other exposures. The screening is provided to every Veteran enrolled in VA health care initially and then at least once every 5 years. Veterans not enrolled but who meet eligibility requirements can also enroll to receive the screening. After the screening, Veterans receive information about benefits, registry exams, and clinical resources they may need. Veterans can request the screening at their VA health care appointment, contact their local VA facility, or schedule a telehealth screening via the VET-HOME website¹.

**Sources:**
¹ [Toxic exposure screenings - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#toxicexposurescreenings)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Toxic exposure screenings](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Toxic Exposure and Hazardous Materials](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [See Also](https://www.veteransbenefitskb.com/agentorange#seealso)

**Confidence:** 0.6662247180938721

### Question 239: PACT-9

**Query:** Can survivors get PACT Act benefits?

**Category:** PACT

**Response Time:** 2.9s

**Answer:**

Yes, survivors of Veterans may be eligible for PACT Act-related benefits. These benefits include:

- A monthly VA Dependency and Indemnity Compensation (DIC) payment if you are the surviving spouse, dependent child, or parent of a Veteran who died from a service-connected disability.
- A one-time accrued benefits payment if you are the surviving spouse, dependent child, or dependent parent of a Veteran who was owed unpaid benefits at the time of their death.
- A Survivors Pension if you are the surviving spouse or child of a Veteran with wartime service.

Survivors can apply for these benefits and may also submit a new application if a previous DIC claim was denied but they believe they are now eligible.

**Sources:**
¹ [Information for survivors - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#informationforsurvivors)  
² [The PACT Act and your VA benefits](https://www.va.gov/resources/the-pact-act-and-your-va-benefits/#pactact)

### Question 241: LEJEUNE-1

**Query:** What is Camp Lejeune water contamination?

**Category:** LEJEUNE

**Response Time:** 1.87s

**Answer:**

Camp Lejeune water contamination refers to the exposure to toxic chemicals found in the drinking water at Marine Corps Base Camp Lejeune and Marine Corps Air Station (MCAS) New River, North Carolina, during the period from August 1, 1953, to December 31, 1987. Veterans, family members, and others who lived, worked, or were otherwise exposed at these locations during that time may be eligible for disability compensation, health care benefits, and other relief due to health conditions linked to this contamination¹.

**Sources:**
¹ [Camp Lejeune Water Contamination - (presumptive)](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#camplejeunewatercontamination)

### Question 242: LEJEUNE-2

**Query:** Am I eligible for Camp Lejeune benefits?

**Category:** LEJEUNE

**Response Time:** 9.81s

**Answer:**

You may be eligible for Camp Lejeune benefits if you meet certain service or family member requirements related to exposure to contaminated water at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River, North Carolina, between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987.

### For Veterans, Reservists, and National Guard members:
You may qualify for VA disability compensation on a presumptive basis if:
- You served at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River for at least 30 days total between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987, **and**
- You did not receive a dishonorable discharge when you separated from the military, **and**
- You have a diagnosis of one or more of the following presumptive conditions:
  - Adult leukemia
  - Aplastic anemia and other myelodysplastic syndromes
  - Bladder cancer
  - Kidney cancer
  - Liver cancer
  - Multiple myeloma
  - Non-Hodgkin’s lymphoma
  - Parkinson’s disease¹³

### For family members:
You may be eligible for health care cost payment or reimbursement related to certain conditions if:
- You are or were a family member (birth or adopted child, married spouse, or legal dependent) of a Veteran who served at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River, **and**
- You lived (or were in utero while your mother lived) at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River for at least 30 days total between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987, **and**
- You apply for and are approved for benefits under current law

Covered conditions for family members include:
- Bladder cancer
- Breast cancer
- Esophageal cancer
- Female infertility
- Hepatic steatosis
- Kidney cancer
- Leukemia
- Lung cancer
- Miscarriage
- Multiple myeloma
- Myelodysplastic syndromes
- Neurobehavioral effects
- Non-Hodgkin’s lymphoma
- Renal toxicity
- Scleroderma²

### Health care benefits for Veterans:
If you meet the service requirements, you may be eligible to enroll in VA health care. For the 15 covered health conditions listed above, you won’t have to pay a copay for care related to those conditions¹.

If you want to file a claim for disability compensation, you need to provide:
- Military records showing you served at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River for at least 30 days between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987
- Medical records showing you have one or more of the 8 presumptive conditions for Veterans³⁶

**Summary:**  
- Veterans must have served at Camp Lejeune/MCAS New River for 30+ days during the specified period, not have a dishonorable discharge, and have a qualifying diagnosis.  
- Family members must have lived or been in utero at Camp Lejeune/MCAS New River for 30+ days during the specified period and be approved for benefits.  
- Both groups have specific covered conditions for benefits eligibility.

**Sources:**
¹ [Am I eligible for VA disability compensation?](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#amieligibleforvadisabilitycompensation)  
² [Benefits for families who lived at Camp Lejeune](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#benefitsforfamilieswholivedatcamplejeune)  
³ [How do I file a claim for disability compensation?](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#howdoifileaclaimfordisabilitycompensation)  
⁴ [Can I also get health care benefits?](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#canialsogethealthcarebenefits)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Can I also get health care benefits?](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Benefits for families who lived at Camp Lejeune](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Am I eligible for VA disability compensation?](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Camp Lejeune Water Contamination](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [On this page](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [How do I file a claim for disability compensation?](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

### Question 243: LEJEUNE-3

**Query:** What conditions are presumptive for Camp Lejeune?

**Category:** LEJEUNE

**Response Time:** 3.67s

**Answer:**

The presumptive conditions for Camp Lejeune, which qualify for VA disability compensation, are:

- Adult leukemia  
- Aplastic anemia and other myelodysplastic syndromes  
- Bladder cancer  
- Kidney cancer  
- Liver cancer  
- Multiple myeloma  
- Non-Hodgkin’s lymphoma  
- Parkinson’s disease  

These conditions are linked to exposure to chemicals in the drinking water at Camp Lejeune and MCAS New River between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987.

Additionally, for VA health care benefits (which may include no copay for care), there are 15 covered conditions related to Camp Lejeune, which include the above plus others such as breast cancer, esophageal cancer, female infertility, hepatic steatosis, lung cancer, miscarriage, neurobehavioral effects, renal toxicity, and scleroderma⁴.

### Question 245: LEJEUNE-5

**Query:** Can family members get Camp Lejeune benefits?

**Category:** LEJEUNE

**Response Time:** 4.23s

**Answer:**

Yes, family members who lived at Camp Lejeune can get VA benefits if they meet all of the following requirements:

- They must be a family member of a Veteran who served at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River, North Carolina (this includes birth or adopted children, married spouses, or other legal dependents).
- They must have lived (or been in utero while their mother lived) at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River for at least 30 days total between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987.
- They must apply for and be approved for benefits under current law.

The VA may pay for or reimburse health care costs related to specific conditions linked to Camp Lejeune water contamination, including bladder cancer, breast cancer, esophageal cancer, female infertility, hepatic steatosis, kidney cancer, leukemia, lung cancer, miscarriage, multiple myeloma, myelodysplastic syndromes, neurobehavioral effects, non-Hodgkin’s lymphoma, renal toxicity, and scleroderma¹.

To apply, family members need to fill out the Camp Lejeune Family Member Program Application (VA Form 10-10068) and send it by mail or fax¹.

**Sources:**
¹ [Benefits for families who lived at Camp Lejeune](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#benefitsforfamilieswholivedatcamplejeune)

**Sources Cited:**
- [Benefits for families who lived at Camp Lejeune](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Can I also get health care benefits?](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [Camp Lejeune Water Contamination](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)
- [On this page](https://veteransbenefitskb.com)

### Question 246: LEJEUNE-6

**Query:** How do I file a Camp Lejeune claim?

**Category:** LEJEUNE

**Response Time:** 5.93s

**Answer:**

To file a Camp Lejeune claim for disability compensation, follow these steps:

- File a new claim online, by mail, in person, or with the help of a trained professional.
- When filing, clearly state that you are applying for one or more of the presumptive conditions related to Camp Lejeune.
- Provide supporting evidence with your claim, including:
  - Military records showing you served at Camp Lejeune or MCAS New River for at least 30 days total between August 1, 1953, and December 31, 1987.
  - Medical records showing you have one or more of the 8 Camp Lejeune presumptive conditions.

You can file online through the VA website or submit VA Form 21-526EZ by mail, fax, or in person at a VA Regional Office. The mailing address for claims is:

```
Department of Veterans Affairs  
Claims Intake Center  
PO Box 4444  
Janesville, WI 53547-4444
```

For assistance, you may also use a Veterans Service Officer (VSO) to help with your claim.

For family members seeking benefits related to Camp Lejeune exposure, there is a separate application process using VA Form 10-10068.

If you want to file for relief under the Camp Lejeune Justice Act of 2022 (PACT Act), you or your legal representative must file an administrative claim with the Department of the Navy.

**Sources:**
¹ [How do I file a claim for disability compensation?](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#howdoifileaclaimfordisabilitycompensation)

⁴ [Benefits for families who lived at Camp Lejeune](https://www.va.gov/disability/eligibility/hazardous-materials-exposure/camp-lejeune-water-contamination/#benefitsforfamilieswholivedatcamplejeune)
